# Task Manager — Project Backlog

Living feature backlog. Updated every session. Claude Code must update this
file whenever a feature is completed or a new issue is discovered. Items are
moved between sections, never deleted. Detailed shipping receipts (test counts,
SHA history, design decisions) live in commit messages and `docs/adr/`; this
file is the index pointer.

---

_(nothing in flight)_

## Completed

- [x] **Dedup calendar.js task-<li> builder into _makeTaskLi (jscpd #228b finding) (#305)** —
  jscpd 5 (bumped in #303) flagged a real 37-line duplicate in `static/calendar.js`
  (day-cell task loop ↔ `_makeUnscheduledLi`) — byte-identical except one line
  (`_dragSourceDate = iso` vs `= null`, which drives move-between-days vs
  reschedule). Extracted a shared `_makeTaskLi(t, sourceDate)` builder; the day
  cell calls `_makeTaskLi(t, iso)` and `_makeUnscheduledLi` becomes a thin
  `_makeTaskLi(t, null)` wrapper. sw.js v224→v225; jscpd now 0 duplication.
  Completed 2026-07-17 — merged to main (b039bcb), gates GREEN, Phase 6
  desktop+mobile clean (both task types render, click opens detail, drag toggles
  .dragging, no overflow, 0 console errors), DEPLOY GREEN at b039bcbe (healthz
  all-ok) + 47/47 prod smoke + 0 server ERROR rows. (Validator cookie had expired
  the day before — minted a fresh one via `railway run mint_validator_cookie.py`
  to run the prod smoke; unrelated to the change. Surfaced a validate_deploy.py
  Windows cp1252 crash when printing the cookie-refresh banner — separate fix.)

- [x] **Close the per-file coverage drift on app.py + digest_api.py (add tests, don't rebaseline) (#304)** —
  Weekly coverage audit (2026-07-17) flagged `app.py` (90.2→80.3%) and
  `digest_api.py` (100→89.7%). Both were real untested code, not flakiness:
  `digest_api.py` lines 67-69 = the `/api/digest/send` `except → record fail →
  raise` transport-error path (added #286/#289, never tested); `app.py`'s big
  uncovered block (751-809) = the #297 `mint-`/`revoke-voice-action-token` Flask
  CLI commands (ADR-034 security tooling shipped without tests). Fixed by ADDING
  tests (not rebaselining, which would just bless the gap): 1 API test that makes
  `send_digest` raise and asserts a `fail` result is recorded + re-raised; 6
  `test_cli_runner` tests for mint (happy / no-SECRET_KEY / no-email) + revoke
  (new jti / append-to-existing / idempotent). Re-measured: digest_api.py → 100%
  (0 missing); app.py → 87.4% (2.8pp drop, within the 5pp tolerance) — both no
  longer flagged. Test-only — no runtime/app code touched (no deploy). Completed
  2026-07-14 — gates GREEN.

- [x] **Clearer audit emails (all 4) via shared renderer + dependency bumps (cryptography 49, jscpd 5) (#303)** —
  User flagged the weekly tech-debt email still used the old terse format (#302
  only reached bug-pattern) and OK'd the two dependency-drift findings.
  (1) New shared renderer `scripts/audit_email.py` — one `render()` builds the
  self-explanatory format (WHAT-THIS-IS preamble, per-check descriptions,
  per-finding blocks, compact "clean this run" list, numbered WHAT-TO-DO;
  weekly/monthly cadence + optional subject/header extras). Retrofitted all 4
  audits (bug-pattern, tech-debt, coverage, security-posture) to call it —
  bug-pattern output byte-identical (tests unchanged); the other 3 get the
  clearer format for the first time. One renderer (vs inlining ×4) also avoids a
  self-inflicted code-duplication finding; imported via the existing `from
  scripts import audit_email` pattern (verified in the standalone run path).
  +`tests/test_audit_email.py` + updated the 3 audits' body assertions.
  (2) Deps: `cryptography 48.0.1→49.0.0` (runtime Fernet lib) + `jscpd
  4.2.4→5.0.12` (dev tool). Completed 2026-07-14 — merged to main (0b06f77),
  gates GREEN, DEPLOY GREEN at 0b06f77 (`encryption ok` confirms cryptography 49
  live) + 5-min monitor clean + 47/47 prod smoke; post-ship `workflow_dispatch`
  confirmed the new clearer tech-debt email + dependency-drift now 0. NOTE:
  jscpd 5 detects better and now surfaces a real pre-existing 37-line
  `calendar.js` duplication (162-198 ↔ 383-4xx) — separate low-priority cleanup.

- [x] **Bug-pattern scan: nested-minmax false positives + clearer alert email + `.sf-sched` wrap (#302)** —
  Triggered by a weekly bug-pattern alert flagging 4 `bare-1fr-grids` findings
  ("is this a bug in the email?"). 3 of 4 were **scanner false positives** —
  `_track_uses_bare_1fr`'s `minmax([^)]+)` strip stopped at the inner `)` of a
  nested `min(300px, 100%)`, exposing the harmless max-slot `1fr` and flagging
  the safe responsive-card idiom `repeat(auto-fill, minmax(min(Npx,100%),1fr))`.
  Fixes: (1) scanner — nesting-aware `_MINMAX_RE` strips one level of nested
  parens (card grids pass; bare `1fr`/`repeat(N,1fr)` still trip); dead
  `_MINMAX_ZERO_RE` removed; +regression tests. (2) `.sf-sched` `repeat(3,1fr)`
  → `repeat(3, minmax(0,1fr))` (the one legit low-risk finding; visually
  identical, overflow-safe; sw.js v223→v224). (3) rewrote `send_scan_email` for
  clarity — "WHAT THIS IS" preamble (advisories not failures; a *missing*
  weekly email is the real signal), plain-English `CHECK_DESCRIPTIONS`,
  per-finding `file:line`+code+`FIX:`, only-fired-checks detail blocks, numbered
  "WHAT TO DO". Scanner+email CI-only; `.sf-sched` the sole UI change. Completed
  2026-07-14 — merged to main (3971065), gates GREEN, Phase 6 desktop+mobile
  clean (3 equal cols, no overflow, no clipped labels), DEPLOY GREEN at 3971065e
  + 5-min monitor clean + 47/47 prod smoke; real style.css now reports 0
  bare-1fr findings; a post-ship `workflow_dispatch` confirmed the new clean-run
  email format live.

- [x] **Strength Forge — mid-workout progress autosave + resistance-only fields (#301)** —
  User-reported friction on the #287 per-set **✎ Log details** form ("I am not able to
  save the progress … exercises that have no resistance shouldn't have a field").
  (1) **On-device draft autosave** — form state debounced to `localStorage`
  (`sf-logdraft:v1:<plan>`) as you type; reopening restores it with a "↩ Picked up your
  in-progress workout" banner + **Start fresh** discard; final button is now **✓ Finish
  & save workout** (POST + clear draft). Works offline; drafts >24h ignored via
  `isDraftFresh`. (2) **Resistance field only on band moves** — bodyweight/stretch/
  breathing exercises render no resistance input (log form) or write-in cell (print
  sheet), driven by a `resist` catalog flag + per-plan-item override (Band Glute Bridge
  in Bands A takes a band). Client-only (server already accepts reps-only sets). New
  dual-export helpers `usesResistance` + `isDraftFresh` (Jest-tested); sw.js v222→v223;
  docs.html Strength section updated. Chose auto-save + hide-resistance-only per operator
  (AskUserQuestion 2026-07-12). Completed 2026-07-12 — merged to main (6630de1), gates
  GREEN, Phase 6 desktop+mobile clean (draft save/restore/finish/start-fresh verified
  end-to-end; end-to-end save persisted reps-only cat-cow `resist=null` + band-squat
  `resist=Medium`; Band Glute Bridge override + Military all-bodyweight verified; no
  overflow; 44px inputs), DEPLOY GREEN at 6630de14 + 5-min monitor clean + 47/47 prod
  smoke.

- [x] #39: Force LF line endings for `.githooks/*` (cross-platform hook bug) — completed 2026-04-22 (SHA cab0c5b). The native gitleaks pre-commit hook from #17 silently broke on every Mac checkout (`env: bash\r: No such file or directory`) because `.githooks/pre-commit` is extension-less and fell through `.gitattributes`'s default `* text=auto` rule, letting Windows autocrlf rewrite the shebang to CRLF. Added explicit `.githooks/* text eol=lf` rule + `git add --renormalize .` (no other diffs — repo was already clean). Regression guard: 6 new tests in `tests/test_repo_hygiene.py` reading working-tree bytes directly. ADR-027.

- [x] #214: Cross-tab task sync — `/calendar` (and `/tasks`) re-render automatically after a mutation on a sibling tab — completed 2026-05-24 (SHA 475480d). User-requested 2026-05-24: "any changes made on the task page need to automatically be reflected on the calendar view". Before: each tab only re-fetched on its own visibilitychange (#114) or 60s poll (#115) — a /calendar tab left open would show stale tier placement after a /tasks PATCH until the user tabbed back. **Fix:** `static/api_client.js` now opens ONE shared `BroadcastChannel("taskmanager:tasks-changed")` and posts on every successful task-affecting mutation (`POST|PATCH|PUT|DELETE` against `/api/(tasks|recurring|projects|goals)`). `subscribeTasksChanged(handler)` exposed for in-tab listeners — `static/calendar.js` calls `renderCalendar()`, `static/app.js` calls the standard loaders bundle. 150ms debounce coalesces a burst (bulk apply, auto-categorize Apply-all) into one re-render. **Why ONE shared instance, not one per file:** `BroadcastChannel` auto-skips self-delivery only within a single instance — two instances in the same tab WOULD see each other's posts, looping a local PATCH into a board re-render and wiping in-DOM state like bulk-select checkboxes (caught by Playwright `tests/e2e/pages.spec.js` `Bulk move-up / move-down`). Post side and subscribe side share the api_client-owned instance so same-tab is a no-op, cross-tab still fires. **Node guard:** Node 15+ ships BroadcastChannel as a global; api_client.test.js runs `testEnvironment: "node"`. A `typeof window !== "undefined"` guard inside `_getOrCreateBus` prevents Jest from opening a real channel that keeps the event loop alive (Jest hangs on exit). CACHE_VERSION v150→v151. Drag-and-drop tier inference on /calendar already lands correctly: cell drop PATCHes `{due_date: iso}`, unscheduled drop PATCHes `{due_date: null}` — `task_service._auto_promote_tier_on_due_today` then routes tier from due_date when tier wasn't in the payload + task isn't frozen + status is ACTIVE (today→TODAY, tomorrow→TOMORROW, this Mon-Sat→THIS_WEEK, next Mon-Sat→NEXT_WEEK, else→BACKLOG). Pre-deploy ALL 15 GATES GREEN (pytest 287 + cov, jest 287, Playwright local 39 + 6 SW + 39 mobile incl. the previously-failing bulk move-up :949 PASS at both desktop and mobile, bandit, pip-audit, npm audit, docs/arch sync, semgrep, gitleaks); post-deploy DEPLOY GREEN at 475480d1 with auth + error-log scan PASS + 5-min monitor clean + 37/37 prod Playwright smoke.

| 240 | **`tests/test_weekly_review.py` — date-drift between `date.today()` (UTC on CI) and `local_today_date()` (DIGEST_TZ on server) breaks `last_reviewed` assertions around midnight ET** | 2026-05-27 | User-reported 2026-05-27 spotted in the failed first run of the #229 coverage audit on GitHub Actions: `tests/test_weekly_review.py::TestReviewFreezeAction::test_freeze_moves_to_freezer` and `test_snooze_stamps_last_reviewed` failed with `'2026-05-26' == '2026-05-27'`. Root cause: tests used `date.today()` (returns the runner's local date — UTC on GitHub Actions) but the server stamps `last_reviewed` via `utils.local_today_date()` which respects `DIGEST_TZ` (America/New_York by default). At any moment between midnight UTC and midnight ET (~5 hours/day in EST, 4 hours in EDT), the two return DIFFERENT dates and the equality assertion fails. Latent since #181 (2026-05-09) which fixed the same class elsewhere but missed this file. The new #229 coverage audit's first CI run was the gate that surfaced it — the audit was DOING ITS JOB (the test failures it surfaced are real, not a workflow bug). **Fix**: route all date arithmetic in `test_weekly_review.py` through a `_today()` helper that wraps `local_today_date()`. Both seed-data lines (`last_reviewed=_today() - timedelta(days=8)`) AND assertions (`body["task"]["last_reviewed"] == _today().isoformat()`) now use the same TZ as the server. `date.today()` no longer imported. Local 33/33 weekly-review tests pass; gates all green. ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-27 (SHA aeee4ef7). | 235 | **`/architecture` Mermaid diagrams render as raw text (`flowchart LR ...`) instead of SVG — broken for every user with the Service Worker active** | 2026-05-25 | User-reported 2026-05-25 with iPhone screenshot: the "AT A GLANCE" and "MORE DETAIL" cards on `/architecture` display the raw Mermaid source (`flowchart LR You((You)) -->|browser| Web[Web app] ...`) instead of the rendered SVG flowcharts. **Root cause**: `static/sw.js` `fetch` handler intercepted EVERY non-API GET — including cross-origin requests to `https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/...` for the Mermaid ES module. Without the module, the `mermaid.contentLoaded()` call at the bottom of `templates/architecture.html` never ran, so the `<pre class="mermaid">` blocks stayed as raw text. **RCA — how this passed validation**: the prod-smoke test `tests/e2e-prod/smoke.spec.js` "architecture page renders Mermaid diagrams" navigated to `/architecture?nosw=1` — the `?nosw=1` query param explicitly unregisters the Service Worker for that page load. So the test exercised the no-SW path (which always worked) and never the actual-user SW path (which was broken). Phase 6 had the same gap: dev-bypass disables Talisman/CSP AND uses `?nosw=1` for Preview. **Bug #55 (2026-04-25)** explicitly called this class out — "Phase 6 limitation — `?nosw=1` masks SW + CSP differences from prod" — and the documented mitigation was "prod-side smoke test asserts the rendered output". We had the prod-side test, but it ALSO used `?nosw=1`, defeating its own purpose. **Fix shipped (#235)**: SW `fetch` handler early-returns for any request whose `url.origin !== self.location.origin` so cross-origin URLs go through the browser's native network stack. ES module imports, third-party fonts, future CDN-loaded assets all bypass the SW cleanly. CACHE_VERSION bumped v166→v167 so users get the fixed SW. **Regression guard added**: NEW prod-smoke test "renders Mermaid diagrams WITH the Service Worker active" navigates WITHOUT `?nosw=1`, exercising the real user path. Without the v167 SW fix, this test fails with a timeout waiting for `pre.mermaid svg`. The existing `?nosw=1` test is kept (it validates the no-SW path is still working). Also NEW local-Playwright SW test `#235 SW does NOT intercept cross-origin requests` uses `page.route` interception to assert the SW correctly skips cross-origin URLs (page.route only fires if the browser saw the request natively — confirming the SW didn't handle it). **Drive-by**: the original `nosw=1`-only test docstring updated with the RCA + cross-reference to the SW-active companion test so future maintainers don't accidentally re-introduce the same gap. | 2026-05-25 | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-25 (SHA b414ba25). | 219 | **`/calendar` duplicate-weeks rendering — current week + next week + current week again from concurrent renderCalendar race** — User-reported 2026-05-24 immediately after #218 went live (screenshot showed Mon May 18–Sun May 24 + Mon May 25–Sun May 31 + a THIRD row Mon May 18–Sat May 23 piling on at the bottom). Root cause: `renderCalendar()` in `static/calendar.js` is `async` and awaits two `apiFetch` calls (`/api/tasks` + `/api/recurring/previews?...`). Multiple firing sources can invoke it concurrently — `visibilitychange` (#114), `apiClient.subscribeTasksChanged` from #214, and the 60s `setInterval` poll (#160). The function called `grid.innerHTML = ""` AT THE TOP, then awaited two network requests, then synchronously appended 2 rows. If a second call started while the first was mid-await, both would clear the grid early (no-op for the second), both would await their fetches, then both would append rows — net effect 4 rows (call A's 2 + call B's 2). Visible the moment a user landed on /calendar with cross-tab activity or visibilitychange firing during the network round-trips. **Fix**: monotonic `_renderGeneration` counter — each `renderCalendar` entry increments and snapshots its own value; after the awaits, if a newer call has bumped the counter, bail before mutating the DOM. The `innerHTML = ""` clear also moved to AFTER the awaits so clear-and-append happen atomically in one synchronous block. Same pattern as the PR67 #132 retry guard. **Regression test**: `tests/e2e/pages.spec.js Calendar concurrent-render race (#219)` fires 5 `window.renderCalendar()` calls via Promise.all and asserts exactly 14 cells AND exactly 2 .calendar-row containers (the user's screenshot symptom). Verified to catch the bug — temporarily reverted my fix and the test failed with `Expected: 14 / Received: <larger>`; with fix re-applied both chromium AND chromium-mobile pass. | 218 | **`/calendar` missing Sunday + tasks moved to next-week tier rendering as "yesterday" — orphan Sunday-dated tasks** — User-reported 2026-05-24 (Sunday) with screenshot showing two calendar rows Mon May 18→Sat May 23 + Mon May 25→Sat May 30 — Sunday May 24 (today!) absent from BOTH rows, AND many tasks the user had moved to "next week" appearing in the previous week's Saturday column. Root cause: the original #72 design treated the work week as Mon-Sat (6 days, Sunday as a planning/rest pivot day with no panel home). That design propagated into THREE behaviors: (a) `/calendar` rendered 6 cells per week × 2 weeks = 12 cells, never showing Sunday; (b) home-board day-strip rendered 12 cells likewise; (c) `task_service._tier_for_due_date` (and its JS mirror `tier_helpers.tierForDueDate`) used `this_monday..this_monday+5` and `next_monday..next_monday+12` (Mon-Sat ranges), so any Sunday due_date fell outside both windows and was orphaned to BACKLOG. The user-reported "tasks moved to next week showing as yesterday" was a downstream visual confusion of the 6-day calendar layout — the top row (visible week 1) was the just-ENDED Mon-Sat from a Sunday viewpoint, making it easy to drag a task onto the wrong Saturday. **And the test suite codified the buggy state**: `tests/e2e-prod/smoke.spec.js:260` asserted `expect(cellCount).toBe(12)` with comment "12 cells (Mon–Sat × 2 weeks per #72)" — the test mirrored design intent, not user expectation, so a future fixer would have failed those tests and assumed they broke something. That's the anti-pattern #3 inverse: codified bugs are worse than no test because they actively resist correction. **Fix (user-confirmed)**: switch to Mon-Sun ISO week, week-starts-Monday. On a Sunday "today," THIS_WEEK ends today (today IS the Sunday cap); NEXT_WEEK is the upcoming Mon-Sun. 12 files touched: `static/calendar.js` (loop `dow < 6` → `< 7`), `static/style.css` (`.calendar-row` grid 6→7 cols, `.day-strip` grid 12→14 cols), `static/app.js` (`_tierDateRange` thisSaturday→thisSunday +6, nextSaturday→nextSunday +13; day-strip render `i < 12` → `< 14` with simplified offset math), `static/tier_helpers.js` (JS mirror), `task_service.py` (Python `_tier_for_due_date` source-of-truth), `static/sw.js` (CACHE_VERSION v153→v154), `templates/docs.html` (Mon–Sat semantics section rewritten as Mon–Sun ISO; tier list, day-strip + /calendar copy updated 12→14 cells), `templates/index.html` (day-strip jinja comment), `ARCHITECTURE.md` (/calendar entry). Tests: `tests/js/unit/tier_helpers.test.js` (describe renamed; new Sun-in-this_week + Sun-in-next_week + Sunday-today edge cases that lock in the fix), `tests/e2e-prod/smoke.spec.js` (`toBe(12)` → `toBe(14)` with comment calling out the codified-bug pattern), `tests/test_promote_due_today.py` (NEW `TestTierForDueDate` class with 12 boundary tests mirroring the Jest cases — locks JS↔Python parity via `monkeypatch` on `_local_today_date`). | 230 | **Complete/cancel on a recurring task with subtasks should NOT close or cancel all subtasks** — User-requested 2026-05-25: "when a reoccuring task has subtasks, if you cancel or complete, it shouldn't close or cancel all the subtasks." For recurring spawns, **silently** archive/cancel the parent + leave subtasks ACTIVE. No prompt. Subtasks become independent from that point, with the parent-link badge in their detail panel showing the now-archived parent name for "where did this come from?" context. Rationale: subtasks of a recurring task ("hand off X, follow up with Y" under a "Weekly Work Prep") often represent independent work that should survive the parent's weekly close-out; cascading was forcing the user to either auto-archive still-relevant work or keep the parent open after they were done with it. **Implementation**: ~6-line early-return in both `complete_parent_task` and `cancel_parent_task` (`task_service.py`). When `task.recurring_task_id is not None`, set status (+ optional cancellation_reason for cancel path), commit, return. Don't compute `open_subtasks`, don't raise ValidationError, don't iterate to archive children. **Side-effect to be aware of**: orphaned subtasks (parent_id pointing at an archived/cancelled parent) accumulate over time. They show on the standard board; close individually. 6 new tests in `TestRecurringSpawnSkipsSubtaskCascade` (`tests/test_tasks_api.py`) including regression guards proving non-recurring parents STILL prompt. **Test-suite debugging note**: the initial end-to-end test draft used `authed_client.get("/api/tasks")` which leaked a Flask test-client session cookie across files; pytest's alphabetical order put `test_tasks_api.py` before `test_validator_cookie.py` and the validator-cookie tamper test's `assert 401` started failing as `200` because the leftover session was satisfying the route. | 207 | **Capture bar ignores `@`-tokens — `@project` "auto-categorize" advertised in code comment but never implemented** — User-reported 2026-05-22. User typed `TPC Update Tracking (@Audit)` into the capture bar expecting `@Audit` to auto-categorize the task; instead the literal `(@Audit)` stayed in the title and the task landed in Inbox with no grouping. **Root cause (code read):** `static/parse_capture.js` is the single source of truth for capture parsing and handles ONLY `#`-hashtags — repeat (`#daily/#weekly/...`), type (`#work/#personal`), tier (`#today/#week/...`), plus URL detection. It has **zero `@`-token handling**. **Secondary bug feeding the confusion:** `static/capture.js:73` carries a stale comment `// --- Parse hashtags, @project, and URLs ---` and `:76` claims "the pure parsing logic is importable by Jest" — both advertise `@project` parsing. `git log -S '@project'` traces the comment to the original UI commit `90724c9` (2026-04-05, "Add main UI"): `@project` was *planned* in that first commit but the parser never implemented it. The `/docs` capture-hints page (lines 81–155) correctly documents only hashtags — so only the code comment is wrong. **Data-model context:** a Task has `project_id` → `Project(name)` (`models.py:181,185,236`); `create_task` (`task_service.py:266,288`) accepts `project_id` only as a UUID — there is no by-name resolution. The natural target for `@<name>` is project assignment, but Tasks have no free-text tag/label field. **Architecture note for whoever implements:** `parseCapture` is a pure client-side function with no knowledge of project names — resolving `@Audit` → a `project_id` needs either (a) the client to fetch the project list and resolve locally, or (b) `parseCapture` to extract the raw `@token` and send it as a `project_name` field that the server resolves case-insensitively in `create_task` (cleaner — single source of truth, mirrors the rest of the API). **Decision deferred** (user 2026-05-22 chose "file the bug, decide later"): (1) what `@<name>` maps to — Project (recommended, fits the model), a new task `tag` column (bigger change), or Goal; (2) no-match behavior — keep token in title silently, surface a warning, or auto-create the project; (3) match precision — exact vs prefix vs fuzzy. **Minimum fix regardless of the decision:** correct/remove the `capture.js:73` + `:76` stale comment so the code stops advertising behavior that doesn't exist. (a) The SW's CLEAR_CACHE handler did NOT wrap its `cache.delete` chain in `event.waitUntil`, so the SW lifecycle didn't block on completion. (b) Even with waitUntil, the SW's fetch handler immediately re-populated the cache via `caches.open(CACHE_NAME).put(...)` whenever any subsequent asset request came through — racing the test's 1s wait. | 181 | **Reflection-apply silently clears project/goal FK when Claude hallucinates a stale name** — Filed 2026-05-20 (audit). `_apply_task_link_hints` (`reflection_service.py:746-758`) translates `project_hint`/`goal_hint` from a Claude UPDATE suggestion via `_resolve_ref`. When the hint doesn't match any active project/goal, `_resolve_ref` returns None — the payload becomes `{..., "project_id": None, "goal_id": None}`. `update_task` honors explicit None as "clear this field" — so the task's existing project_id is silently CLEARED on apply. Same #57-class silent payload drop, but originating from server-side AI instead of the client. User sees the project disappear with no error in the summary. **Fix sketch:** when `_resolve_ref` returns None for a hint, `pop` the key entirely instead of setting it to None — `update_task`'s "absent field = no change" semantics then preserves the original value. Append `summary["errors"].append("project_hint <X> not found, kept existing project")` so the user sees what happened. **Effort:** XS. | 2026-05-20 | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-21 (PR 6, SHA 1b0c26c0). `_apply_task_link_hints` now: a hint that resolves sets the id; a hint that does NOT resolve has its key popped entirely (`update_task`'s "absent key = no change" preserves the original FK); a non-empty unresolved hint appends `"project_hint 'X' not found — kept the task's existing project"` to `summary["errors"]`. An empty/blank hint is popped silently (just "no hint", not a hallucination, no warning). `_apply_task_link_hints` gained a `summary` parameter for the error surfacing. 3 pytest cases: stale hint keeps existing FK + surfaces miss; resolved hint still sets id (happy path); empty hint silent + no change. Shipped with #174 under PR 6. Pre-deploy ALL GATES GREEN; post-deploy SHA match + monitor clean + 37/37 prod smoke. |

| 56 | **Eliminate post-deploy hard-refresh requirement for users (SW staleness)** — user-flagged 2026-04-25 after #55: "a normal web app shouldn't require this." Diagnosis: existing SW (`static/sw.js` + `templates/base.html` handshake) DOES auto-update via 60s poll + visibility-change + initial load, BUT there's a race window. If a user navigates to a page right after a deploy AND before the handshake has detected the new SW version, the old SW intercepts the request: it serves NEW HTML via network-first, but the page's referenced static assets (CSS/JS) come cache-first from the OLD CACHE_NAME — leaving the user with new-HTML-against-old-static-asset combo. Two fix paths: (A) **drop HTML caching** in the SW entirely — `cache.put` for text/html responses removed; HTML always comes fresh from network. Removes the offline benefit for HTML (questionable since pages need API data anyway) but eliminates the race. (B) **skipWaiting on install** — new SW activates immediately when downloaded; old SW dies. Existing handshake's `userIsBusy()` guard would be removed (or kept as "wait for blur" only). Risk: user mid-edit gets a SW swap-out, possibly losing in-flight requests. (A) is safer + cleaner. | 2026-04-25 | ✅ FIXED 2026-04-24 (SHA 1ed3c94, Path A). HTML caching removed from `static/sw.js`: `text/html` + `/api/` requests now go straight to network, never read or written to cache. `"/"` removed from APP_SHELL pre-cache. CACHE_VERSION bumped v53→v54 so the old SW's HTML cache entries are dropped on activate. Static assets still cache-first. Phase 6 verified at desktop + mobile (no console errors, cache contains only static assets after navigation). DEPLOY GREEN; 6/6 prod smoke pass. Tradeoff accepted: lose offline HTML fallback (pages need API data anyway). |

| 160 | **`/calendar` lags behind state changes — needs more aggressive refresh** — User-reported 2026-05-09 (split-out from closed #152). User saw a stale render of /calendar showing tasks at the wrong cell briefly until they refreshed. The page already has a `visibilitychange` handler (#114) that calls `loadTasks` when the tab is brought back to focus, but that doesn't cover the case where the user makes changes ON /calendar (drag a task between cells, drop on a cell from the Unscheduled aside) and the cell it just left still shows the task for a beat. **Possible fixes:** (a) optimistic local mutation — update the byDate bucket in JS before the PATCH round-trip; (b) re-fetch + re-render on every successful PATCH (currently the page only re-fetches on visibilitychange); (c) websockets / SSE for cross-tab consistency. | 161 | **Tier vs due_date drift — task with tier=tomorrow can have due_date=today (and vice versa)** — Diagnostic-found 2026-05-09 while investigating #152. Task "create intro letters for Ryan" had `tier=tomorrow` and `due_date=2026-05-09` (today, Saturday). The Today panel filters strictly by `tier=today`, so this task was invisible there even though the date said today. Caused by: user manually edits one field without the auto-promote gate firing — `_auto_promote_tier_on_due_today` (`task_service.py:133`) skips when the PATCH includes both `tier` and `due_date`, OR when the user just edits one without touching the other. **Fix proposals:** (a) "Show on both" — the Today panel surfaces tasks where `tier=today` OR `due_date=today` (excluding freezer/inbox); same for Tomorrow. No state mutation, just an inclusive filter on the read side. (b) Mutation-on-read — every list endpoint reconciles tier ↔ due_date and persists. Cleaner state but write-on-read feels gross. (c) Add a "drift warning" badge to tasks where tier and due_date disagree. **Recommend (a) — least invasive, mirrors the calendar's slicing.** | 2026-05-09 | ✅ DONE (shipped earlier; corrected in the 2026-05-22 backlog audit). The Today panel inclusively surfaces the `tier=tomorrow` + `due_date=today` drift case — `static/app.js:615` (`#161` comment, narrowed 2026-05-14 to the tomorrow-roll case) — Option (a). |

| 259 | **DBLogHandler attached twice — every WARNING+ log row duplicates in `app_logs`** | Bug / Logging | Low-Medium | Discovered 2026-05-29 02:30 UTC during the #167 ship: the four boot-time replay WARNINGs each landed as TWO rows in `app_logs` with distinct UUIDs and ~38ms apart (e.g. `cron_audit.replay_missed start tomorrow_roll …` appears at 02:30:35.524948 AND 02:30:35.562433). **Root cause analysis**: with `preload_app=True` in `gunicorn.conf.py`, the master process imports `app:app` → `app = create_app()` runs at module level (under `_RUNNING_UNDER_PYTEST=False` per #248) → `configure_logging()` attaches DBLogHandler #1 to root. Workers fork inheriting the master's logging config (and #1). Then `post_worker_init` in worker 1 calls `create_app()` a SECOND time → `configure_logging()` runs again → DBLogHandler #2 attached. Worker 1's root logger now has TWO DBLogHandlers, so every `logger.warning(...)` produces TWO inserts. **Impact**: app_logs grows ~2× faster than expected; `/api/debug/logs` shows duplicates; the 10k retention cap fills faster. **NOT a correctness issue** — the cron work itself ran once (the `cron_audit` rows have correct rowcount=14/0/14/2 not 28/0/28/4). **Fix shape**: make `configure_logging()` idempotent — check if a `DBLogHandler` is already attached to root and skip if so. Or: skip the duplicate `create_app()` in `post_worker_init` since the master already created the app under preload. **Tests**: add a regression in `test_logging.py` asserting that calling `configure_logging(app)` twice on the same root logger does NOT attach two DBLogHandlers. **Pre-existing**: this bug pre-dates #167. It was invisible until now because pre-#167 the app emitted ~0 WARNINGs per day in steady state; #167's boot replay emits a burst of 9 WARNINGs in the first ~70ms which made the doubling obvious. | XS — one-line idempotency guard + 1 regression test. | Low. | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-29 — idempotency guard added to `configure_logging()` in `logging_service.py:498`: before constructing the new handler, scan `root.handlers` for an existing `DBLogHandler` and return it if found. Root level is still raised if needed (so a higher-verbosity second call still takes effect). Three new pytest cases in `TestConfigureLoggingIdempotent` (`tests/test_logging.py`): (1) two configure calls → exactly 1 DBLogHandler on root (count assertion); (2) two configure calls + one WARNING emit → exactly 1 row in app_logs (end-to-end repro that would have caught the original bug); (3) the second configure call returns the same handler instance (test contract for callers that retain the return value). Each test runs under an `isolate_root_handlers` autouse fixture that snapshots + restores root.handlers + root.level so it can't poison sibling tests. Matches the existing `_logging_hooks_installed` guard pattern for before/after request hooks. End-to-end verified on prod post-deploy at SHA 9aad11e (boot at 03:52:13 UTC): 4 boot-replay WARNINGs landed as SINGLE rows in `app_logs` (vs the doubled pair at 02:30:35.524948 + 02:30:35.562433 on the pre-fix deploy at 6aecc961). Bonus cascade: the 03:52 boot's replay loop correctly read the 02:30 boot's audit rows and SKIPPED all 4 nightly jobs with "reason=already_ran" — confirms #167 + #259 working together. Pre-deploy ALL GATES GREEN. Post-deploy DEPLOY GREEN at 9aad11e3 + Error log scan PASS + 5-min MONITOR GREEN + 39/39 prod Playwright smoke. |
| 167 | **Scheduler self-heal — auto-replay missed midnight crons at container startup** \| Reliability / Ops | Medium-High | User-flagged 2026-05-20 as the follow-up to #166. #166 gives a manual replay path; this item closes the loop so the user never has to remember to run it after a Railway outage. When the container comes up between 00:01 and the next midnight, the scheduler init should detect that one or more of the four midnight jobs (`tomorrow_roll`, `promote_due_today`, `realign_tiers`, `recurring_spawn`) did not fire today and run them inline, exactly once, before normal request traffic begins. The `scheduler_heartbeat` job already writes a `scheduler_heartbeat` row every 45s (`health.write_scheduler_heartbeat`) — pairing each cron fire with its own audit row (`cron_last_run` keyed by `job_id`, columns `last_fire_at`, `last_status`, `last_rowcount`) gives a deterministic "did this fire today?" check. On startup: for each midnight job, if `now() ≥ today's scheduled fire` AND `last_fire_at < today's scheduled fire`, run the helper and write the row. Idempotent because the helpers themselves are idempotent (each `UPDATE … WHERE tier=X` is a no-op the second time). | New `models.CronAudit` table `(job_id PK, last_fire_at, last_status, last_rowcount, last_elapsed_ms)`. New `cron_audit.replay_missed(now=None)` invoked from `_start_digest_scheduler` after `scheduler.start()` that loops over the four jobs in scheduler order and runs any whose `last_fire_at` predates today's scheduled time. Factor `JOB_ORDER` into a shared `cron_jobs.py` so live scheduler + manual script + boot-time auto-replay all share one source of truth. | Small — one new model + one new service module + ~20 lines wiring in `_init_scheduler` + tests. Source-inspection test in test_security (limiter is disabled in tests). |

| 186 | **Client-supplied `X-Request-ID` accepts ASCII control chars → log-line forging** \| Sec | Low | Filed 2026-05-20 (audit). `logging_service.py:413-417` accepts incoming `X-Request-ID` if `len ≤ 64` and `raw.isascii()`. `str.isascii()` returns True for `\n`, `\r`, `\x00`-`\x1f`, `\x7f`. PR62 audit-fix #24 added `_CTRL_CHARS_RE` to scrub control chars from `combined` in `debug_api.client_error` — but the same defense wasn't applied to `request_id`. An attacker can send `X-Request-ID: abc\nfake-line`; the literal `\n` ends up in `app_logs.request_id`, then gets concatenated into the `combined` field on `/api/debug/logs`. JSON display surface prevents HTML re-injection but plain-text terminal log scans can be misled. | Apply `_CTRL_CHARS_RE.sub(" ", raw)` (or stricter `re.match(r"^[A-Za-z0-9._\-]+$")`) to the accepted header before assigning to `g.request_id`. | XS. | Low. | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-22 (PR 9, SHA 158580f1). | 154 | **Backups — database + off-Railway cold storage** | Reliability / Infra | High | User-flagged 2026-05-09: "as there is more and more critical data, I need to consider backups, both of the database and off Railway." (2) retention — keep last 7 daily + last 4 weekly + last 6 monthly? (3) destination — S3 (most pro), Backblaze B2 (cheapest), Dropbox/GDrive (simplest), or git-LFS push to a private GitHub repo (already has GH credentials)? (4) format — `pg_dump --format=custom` (Postgres-specific, smallest) vs SQL text dump (portable, larger) vs JSON export per table (most portable, no Postgres on the restore side)? (5) encryption at rest — Fernet-encrypt the dump before upload? Keys live where? (6) trigger — Railway cron job, GitHub Actions scheduled, or local script? (7) restore drill — quarterly automated round-trip test? | Medium-Large — depends heavily on the answers above. Easiest MVP: daily `pg_dump` on Railway → push to GitHub LFS (free up to 1 GB), Fernet-encrypted with a key stored in 1Password. ~1 day's work. Pro version with S3 + retention rotation: ~2-3 days. | ✅ DONE (shipped earlier; corrected in the 2026-05-22 backlog audit). `scripts/backup_to_github.py` does pg_dump → Fernet-encrypt → push to a private GitHub repo; `.github/workflows/daily-backup.yml` cron + `monthly-restore-drill.yml`; `templates/docs.html` `#backups` section with the 7-step setup guide. User has run the app on mobile for months without filing a tap-accuracy bug, so not ship-blocking, but a real defect. | Design pass at both 375×812 and 1280×800 (so desktop UI doesn't get ugly). | 125 | **`tasks_api.url_preview` SSRF defense has TOCTOU window — drop the duplicate resolution loop** | Tech debt / Sec | Low | Audit 2026-04-30. The route resolves the hostname, IP-checks each result, then calls `safe_fetch_user_url()` which **re-resolves** independently. Between the two resolutions, DNS could rebind. `safe_fetch_user_url()` does pin its own first-resolution IP into the URL so the second hop is safe — but the design intent (route does pre-check, then delegates) leaves the impression that the route's check matters, which it doesn't. Not exploitable today. If someone ever tweaks `safe_fetch_user_url` to take a pre-validated IP from caller, this becomes exploitable. | XS — drop the duplicate resolution loop in `tasks_api.url_preview` (keep just the `safe_fetch_user_url` call). | Low. | ✅ FIXED 2026-04-30 (PR63). New `egress.is_user_url_allowed(url)` helper extracts the IP-allowlist check; `tasks_api.url_preview` now calls `is_user_url_allowed()` for the loud-400 pre-check + `safe_fetch_user_url()` for the actual fetch — both share the same canonical resolution, eliminating the cosmetic TOCTOU window. `socket` and `ipaddress` imports dropped from `tasks_api.py`. |
| 126 | **`APP_DEBUG_TOKEN` scope creep onto mutating `/api/debug/backfill/*` endpoints — split into read + admin tokens** | Sec / Polish | Medium | Audit 2026-04-30. `APP_DEBUG_TOKEN` was originally for read-only log queries. It now also authenticates **mutating** backfill endpoints (`task-goal-from-project`, `realign-tiers`, `today-tomorrow-due-date`, `project-colors`). No expiry; pasted into shell history every use. New `debug_admin_auth_required` decorator and `APP_DEBUG_ADMIN_TOKEN` env var. The 4 mutating endpoints (`task-goal-from-project`, `today-tomorrow-due-date`, `project-colors`, `realign-tiers`) now require the admin token via the header path; OAuth still works for the human developer. The READ token (`APP_DEBUG_TOKEN`) does NOT pass the admin gate — a leaked read token can no longer rewrite tier/goal/project state. Admin token ALSO satisfies the read decorator (admin ⊇ read), so a single admin token works for everything. README updated with both env vars. 5 new tests cover: read token blocked on backfill, admin token grants backfill, admin satisfies read, unset admin blocks header path entirely, realign-tiers covered too. |

| 134 | **Performance audit batch 2: collapse 3 N+1 anti-patterns** | Performance | High + Critical | Found by perf audit 2026-04-30. **#1**: `goals_api._serialize` called `goal_progress(goal.id)` per goal in the list comprehension, firing 3 COUNT queries per goal. ~20 goals = 60 round-trips per /goals load — runs on init + every 60s poll + visibilitychange. **#2**: `task_service.list_tasks` had no eager-loading; `tasks_api._serialize` then accessed `task.subtasks` and `task.recurring_task` lazily, firing 2 SELECTs per task. ~150 active tasks = ~300 extra queries per board load. **#5**: `recycle_service.list_bin` did the same 3-COUNTs-per-batch shape against soft-deleted batches. | XS each. | Low. | ✅ FIXED 2026-04-30 (PR69). | 121 | **OAuth `MismatchingStateError` returns 500 to user** | Bug | High | User-reported 2026-04-28: "Internal Server Error... getting this when i hit the network reconnect button". | 106 | **SW-active Playwright tests hang on `navigator.serviceWorker.ready`** | Bug / Test infra | Medium | Filed 2026-04-27 mid-PR39 (audit E2 partial). | 227 | **Recurring security audit — monthly posture review, not just CVE scan** \| Sec / Audit \| High \| User-flagged 2026-05-24 (one of four "recurring audit" requests). | 237 | **Reflection — persist the raw per-segment Whisper transcriptions alongside the final edited reflection (audit trail)** | Feature / Audit | Medium | User-requested 2026-05-25 immediately after #232 shipped: "for the reflection - please ensure we save the raw transcriptions too if we are not already." Current flow (#232): each `Pause` uploads its audio to `/api/reflection/transcribe-segment` → Whisper returns text → text appended to `#reflText` textarea. The user CAN edit the textarea between segments. On `Done`, only the FINAL merged textarea content is POSTed to `/api/reflection` and persisted as the `Reflection.transcript` — the raw per-segment Whisper output is never saved. If the user edits "I shipped the auth refresh" → "I almost shipped the auth refresh", the original raw Whisper text is lost. **Proposed**: client-side, buffer each segment's transcript in a `rawSegments` array (one entry per successful `/transcribe-segment` call). On Done, send both the merged text AND the raw segments to `/api/reflection` (or a new sibling field on the existing payload). Server-side, add a `Reflection.raw_segments` JSONB column (list of `{text, duration_seconds, cost_usd, recorded_at}`) and persist them. The detail view (`GET /api/reflection/<id>`) returns them; the history page can show a "Raw segments" `<details>` collapsible alongside the existing "Show transcript". **Why it matters**: the user can always see what they originally said vs. what they later edited — important for self-honesty in a reflection feature. Also: in the rare case Claude's analyze pass leans on a specific phrasing, an editing-away of that phrasing breaks the analysis without obvious explanation. **Effort**: S — new DB column (alembic migration), small payload addition to `/api/reflection` POST, small UI toggle on the history view. **Complexity**: Low — additive change, no migration risk for existing rows (default `[]`). | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-26 (SHA f8b18164). Pre-deploy ALL 11 GATES GREEN. Post-deploy DEPLOY GREEN at f8b18164 (alembic migration `e5f6a7b8c9d0` applied cleanly against prod Postgres) + auth + error-log scan PASS + 5-min MONITOR GREEN + 39/39 prod Playwright smoke. New `Reflection.raw_segments` JSONB column (alembic migration `e5f6a7b8c9d0`, server_default `'[]'` so existing rows backfill cleanly). | 225 | **Playwright flake — `pages.spec.js:688` ("dragging a dated task to This Week LEAVES the date alone") times out on `request.get`** — Discovered 2026-05-24 during the #223 ship: test failed with `TimeoutError: apiRequestContext.get: Timeout 10000ms exceeded`. Verified pre-existing on clean `eded3cb` baseline (not introduced by #223). Root cause: the test used a fixed `await page.waitForTimeout(700)` to "wait for the drag's PATCH+reorder to clear" before doing `request.get`. The drop dispatches two server-side calls (PATCH /api/tasks/<id> + POST /api/tasks/reorder) against Flask's single-threaded dev server on SQLite — when those took >700ms (e.g. 14s in the failing case under DBLogHandler-write contention), the subsequent `request.get` queued behind the still-running write transaction and hit its 10s timeout. The sibling Tomorrow test (line 637) happened to fit under 700ms historically but is the same fragility class. **Fix**: replace the fixed `waitForTimeout` with explicit `page.waitForResponse(...)` for both the PATCH and reorder responses, with 15s timeout slack. Applied to both cross-tier tests (Tomorrow + This Week) for consistency. Post-fix verified: Tomorrow 3.2s + This Week 14.6s (the test now correctly waits the 14.6s instead of timing out). **Production note**: the underlying server-side slowness is a test-environment artifact only — Flask dev server + SQLite single-writer-lock. Production runs PostgreSQL with row-level locks (no equivalent contention) AND gunicorn multi-worker (multiple concurrent writers OK). **2026-05-24 follow-up investigation closed**: hypothesized the original 500 on `/api/tasks/reorder` + DBLogHandler insert failures pointed at an underlying server-side bug. Reproduced the exact PATCH→reorder→GET sequence via direct `curl` (no Playwright, no concurrency) — all three calls returned 200 in ~300ms each. So the endpoints are clean. The 500 + DBLogHandler contention in the original failing run was a **cascade of the test race itself**: the test's 10s timeout fired → its `finally` block called `request.delete(/api/tasks/<id>)` → the still-in-flight reorder hit a deleted task → 500 → Flask's `_after_request` logged that 500 at WARNING level → DBLogHandler tried to insert → SQLite writer-lock contention with other concurrent log-inserts → retry → repeat. Once the deterministic wait fix lands (this PR), the race vanishes and so does the entire downstream cascade. No additional code fix needed; the test-infra fix IS the root-cause fix. | 2026-05-24 | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-24 (SHA c008592). Pre-deploy ALL 15 gates green (Playwright local 60+6+60); post-deploy DEPLOY GREEN at c0085922 + auth + error-log scan PASS + 5-min MONITOR GREEN + 38/38 prod Playwright smoke (test-only change, no server impact, but validated for safety). Follow-up investigation closed same day — confirmed root cause was the test race itself, not a server bug. |

| 274 | **Speed up the pre-commit gate suite without sacrificing reliability** | Tooling / Developer Experience | Medium | User-flagged 2026-05-30: "the gates seem to take a long time." Measured breakdown (two real `run_all_gates.sh` runs 2026-05-30): **Playwright local is ~75% of wall-time and 100% serial** — chromium 4.3m + chromium-mobile 4.2m + chromium-sw 1.0m ≈ **9.5m**, because `playwright.config.js` sets `workers: 1`. pytest runs serially with `--cov` (no xdist; pytest-xdist not installed). jest (335) + ruff + bandit + pip-audit + npm-audit + semgrep + gitleaks are each fast. Verify test isolation first (no order-dependence / shared-fixture races). Low-med risk, med win. (2) **Overlap pytest ∥ Playwright** — they're independent processes (pytest standalone; Playwright hits the port-5111 bypass), so run concurrently in `run_all_gates.sh`; saves ~min(pytest, playwright). Low risk. (3) **Playwright worker parallelism for chromium + chromium-mobile** — the BIG win (could ~halve the 8.5m) but BLOCKED by the shared single-SQLite bypass server: parallel workers mutating one DB race. Needs per-worker isolated server+DB instances. Higher effort. (4) **Fan out the fast independent gates** (ruff/jest/security scanners) concurrently — small absolute win, free. (5) **OneDrive + Defender exclusion** for the repo path — the repo lives under OneDrive (same I/O overhead that swallows the pytest pass-count line); excluding the working dir from sync + real-time scan may speed file-heavy collection. | 279 | **Calendar within-cell reorder can collide `sort_order` with same-tier tasks in other cells** | Bug | Low | Surfaced by the 2026-06-01 ad-hoc bug scan (code-reviewer subagent over the session diff). `_reorderWithinCell` (`static/calendar.js`) sends the cell's `task_ids` to `POST /api/tasks/reorder`, which sets `sort_order = 0,1,2…` for exactly those ids. A calendar cell holds tasks of whatever tier happens to fall on that day, so reordering a cell rewrites a *subset* of a tier's sort_order namespace to small integers — which can tie/collide with the same tier's tasks sitting in OTHER day cells, making the board's relative order for that tier ambiguous (tiebreak falls to `created_at DESC`). | **Largely mitigated today** because the only multi-cell tiers (`this_week`/`next_week`) are day-grouped on the board (`DAY_GROUPED_TIERS`, app.js) — each calendar cell maps 1:1 to a board weekday sub-group, so colliding sort_orders live in *different* groups and aren't directly compared; `today`/`tomorrow` are single-cell (no collision) and `backlog`/`freezer` aren't on the calendar. So the visible-bug surface is narrow. **Proper fix:** permute only among the cell tasks' EXISTING sort_order values (reassign the same N slots in the new order) instead of writing 0..N — needs either a new endpoint mode or a client-side value-preserving payload. **Test gap:** the local Playwright reorder test (`pages.spec.js` #267) only covers the same-cell/same-tier happy path; add a cross-cell same-tier case if fixing. | S-M. | Low — narrow repro window; fix touches the shared sort_order semantics. | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-01 (9004699). Fixed with a **full-tier renumber** (better than the value-preserving idea, which couldn't reorder degenerate all-0 slots): when the whole cell is one tier, substitute the cell's tasks (in their new visual order) into the positions they currently occupy in that tier's order, leave every other same-tier task in place, and send the WHOLE tier to /api/tasks/reorder → it renumbers 0..N with every member distinct (no collision); non-cell tasks keep their relative position. Falls back to the cell-only reorder for a mixed-tier cell / cache miss. Substitution math = new pure `reorderTierWithCell(tierOrderedIds, cellNewOrder)` in `calendar_bucket_helpers.js` (6 Jest cases incl. the partial-cell scenario + other-cell-task-stays-put). Behavioral Playwright test (drag-to-bottom → moves down + distinct slots). **Verified live**: after a cell reorder the entire today tier (11 tasks) had distinct sort_orders. Gates green, deploy GREEN + monitor, prod smoke 46/46. |
| 280 | **`#detailMeta` gets "Created: Invalid Date" in create-mode (hidden, latent)** | Bug | Low | Surfaced by the 2026-06-01 ad-hoc bug scan. `taskDetailOpen` (`static/app.js:2459`) unconditionally writes `Created: ${new Date(task.created_at)…}` into `#detailMeta`. When opened via `taskDetailOpenNew` (#269 capture-bar full window + #270 calendar empty-cell create), the stub task has no `created_at`/`updated_at`, so it renders "Created: Invalid Date / Updated: Invalid Date". `_setDetailCreateMode(true)` HIDES `#detailMeta`, so it's invisible to users today — purely latent. | Trivial guard: wrap the meta write in `if (task.id) { … }` (or `if (task.created_at)`). NOTE: a PreToolUse security hook flagged an earlier innerHTML edit on this exact line during #269 — the hook-safe alternative is to clear `detailMeta.textContent = ""` inside `_setDetailCreateMode` when `isCreate`, leaving the innerHTML sink line untouched. | XS. | Low — invisible/latent; 1-line fix. | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-01 (9004699). Rebuilt the meta block with `textContent` + `createElement` (hook-safe — no innerHTML sink) and guarded on `task.id`: create mode (`taskDetailOpenNew`) now leaves `#detailMeta` empty; edit mode still renders Created/Updated. Verified live: edit-mode shows "Created: 6/1/2026 / Updated: 6/1/2026", create-mode meta empty (no Invalid Date). Gates green, deploy GREEN, prod smoke 46/46. |

| 4 | **Recycle bin: TTL cleanup** — auto-purge soft-deleted rows after N days | Infra | Low | Prevents DB bloat — set-and-forget maintenance | Low — one APScheduler job, one env var, one UI countdown | Low — simple scheduled query + "expires in X days" UI | Only after manual cleanup proves insufficient |
| 5 | **TLS certificate expiry check** — warn-only check in `/healthz` | Infra | Very Low | Early warning on cert expiry — but Railway auto-renews, so near-zero risk today | Very Low — one function, TLS socket check | Very Low — well-understood pattern, warn-only | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-01 (PR87, SHA e8dcaa9). New `check_tls_expiry()` in `health.py` opens a TLS socket to a configurable host, reads the peer cert's `notAfter`, and reports days remaining via `/healthz`. Disabled by default — only runs when `TLS_EXPIRY_HOST` env var is set (e.g. `shigs.us` or `shigs.us:443`). Always warn-only (never `fail:`) so an expiring cert can't brick a deploy. Returns: `skipped: TLS_EXPIRY_HOST not set` (default), `ok` (>30 days), `warn: <N> days remaining` (≤30 days), `warn: cert expired N days ago`, or `warn: TLS check failed: <reason>` on DNS / handshake / parse error. 5-minute per-process cache prevents per-probe TLS handshakes during Railway's tight deploy-probe loop. Today's value is near-zero (Railway auto-renews managed TLS) but gives a 30-day heads-up if/when this app moves to self-managed TLS. 9 pytest cases (env unset/blank, invalid port, DNS failure on real .invalid host, mocked socket+ssl for ok / warn / expired / missing notAfter / cache verification). Cascade: README.md env-vars table updated; docs_sync_check + arch_sync_check green; `validate_deploy.py` auto-discovers the new check (no script edit needed). No CACHE_VERSION bump (backend-only). Pre-deploy: 12 gates green. Post-deploy: SHA match, 10/10 healthz, error log scan PASS, monitor clean, 35/35 prod Playwright smoke. Live verified: prod /healthz now reports `tls_expiry: skipped: TLS_EXPIRY_HOST not set` in the auto-emitted Deploy Validation Report. |

| 12 | **AI-assisted triage suggestions** — recommend tier based on task age and patterns | Feature | Medium | Reduce inbox pile-up — AI suggests "this has sat 14 days, freeze or delete?" | Medium — data analysis queries, Claude prompt, accept/dismiss UI | Low-Medium — heuristics are simple (age, tier, patterns); main work is suggestion UI | ✅ RESOLVED 2026-05-01 (PR85, SHA d84eccf) — heuristic v1. New `triage_service.py` (`compute_triage_suggestions()`) + `triage_api.py` (`GET /api/triage/suggestions`) + new section above the existing `/review` card listing stale-task suggestions with one-click Apply / Dismiss buttons. Apply routes through canonical `PATCH /api/tasks` (tier change) or `DELETE /api/tasks` — no separate mutation surface. Heuristics: INBOX > 7 days, TODAY/TOMORROW past due > 3 days, THIS_WEEK > 14 days, NEXT_WEEK > 21 days → move to BACKLOG; BACKLOG > 90 days, FREEZER > 60 days → delete. Subtasks excluded (ride along with parent); deleted/cancelled excluded. Sorted by days_stale desc. The "AI" framing was deliberately de-scoped to heuristic-only: single-user threat model + low API budget make pure-rules right for v1, and 26 days of history isn't enough yet for LLM classification to clearly beat rules. LLM upgrade can come later. 16 pytest cases (one positive + boundary-negative per heuristic + exclusions + sort + API contract); 100% coverage on both new modules. Phase 6 verified at desktop 1280×800 + mobile 375×812 against an injected aged inbox task: empty-state hidden, populated panel renders, Apply moves task and removes row, mobile row stacks vertically with 44px-tall Apply button (#140 floor honored), 0 console errors, no overflow.
